0.1 Editor's Words
0.1 Editor's Words
GRI 2-1、2-2、2-3、2-4、2-14
This report is the fifteenth Sustainability Report published by Everest Textile 
Co., Ltd. (hereinafter referred to as "Everest", "Everest Textile", or "the Company"). 
It is issued annually to ensure ongoing communication with stakeholders. 
The report covers Everest’s performance and activities in 2024 across the 
three pillars of sustainability: Environmental (E), Social (S), and Governance (G). 
Reporting Scope and Calculation Basis
This report follows the principle of consolidated reporting boundaries and 
includes the Company’s four global manufacturing sites—Taiwan, Shanghai, 
Thailand, and North Carolina (USA)—as well as the Taipei Sales Office. Compared 
to the Annual Report, the Ethiopia factory is currently excluded due to 
operational instability and ongoing development of its management information 
system.
Financial performance data are derived from publicly disclosed information 
certified by a CPA. All data collected from January 1, 2024 to December 31, 2024 
is calculated in New Taiwan Dollars (TWD). Environmental performance metrics 
are based on publicly available government data and Everest’s own estimates.
If there are any restatements of historical data compared to the “2023 
Sustainability Report,” explanations will be provided within the text.
Reporting Framework and Guidelines
This report has been prepared in accordance with the GRI Standards 2021 
issued by the Global Reporting Initiative (GRI). It also references the SASB 
(Sustainability Accounting Standards Board) and TCFD (Task Force on Climate-
related Financial Disclosures) frameworks, as well as the “Regulations Governing 
the Preparation and Filing of Sustainability Reports by TWSE Listed Companies” 
issued by the Taiwan Stock Exchange.
The report discloses Everest's 2024 performance on sustainability 
topics, including relevant strategies, targets, actions, and outcomes across 
environmental, social, and governance dimensions.
The 2024 Everest Sustainability Repor t was compiled by the 
ESG Editorial Team, which was responsible for overall planning, 
communication integration, data consolidation, and content editing. All 
content and data were reviewed by team members and submitted for 
Board of Directors' review and approval prior to publication.
External Assurance
This report has been verified by SGS Taiwan Ltd. in accordance with AA1000AS 
v3, Type 1 Moderate Assurance level.
Publication Timeline
Everest publishes its sustainability report annually and makes it publicly 
available on the Everest Global Information Network.
Previous version: Published in June 2024
Current version: Published in June 2025
Report Preparation and Contact Information
You may download the full report from the Everest Global Information 
Network. For any inquiries or suggestions regarding this report, please feel free 
to contact us:
Remarks: This report follows the eight reporting principles outlined in the GRI Universal 
Standards—accuracy, balance, clarity, comparability, completeness, context, timeliness, and 
verifiability.

0.2 Message from the Chairman
0.2 Message from the Chairman
GRI 2-22
The world today is changing rapidly and is full of uncertainties, making it increasingly difficult to predict future developments. Breakthroughs in artificial intelligence (AI), the rapid evolution of green 
technologies, and the accelerated transformation of the new energy industry are reshaping the global landscape. Meanwhile, geopolitical tensions and climate change have emerged as major risks to 
global economic development. Complex events such as the ongoing Russia–Ukraine war, the potential return of Donald Trump to the White House after his 2020 election defeat, and the resurgence of 
the U.S.–China trade war have intensified political turbulence and severely impacted global industrial supply chains, resulting in increased market volatility. Looking ahead to 2025, the global economy 
remains highly unpredictable. U.S. tariff policies may further drive up prices, disrupt supply chains, and weaken real incomes, adding to the risk of greater market uncertainty. At the same time, climate 
change continues to disrupt supply chains and is accelerating the arrival of the carbon tariff era, creating more complex challenges for corporate operations. As climate change exerts a profound global 
impact, net-zero emissions have become a prevailing international goal. Carbon reduction and energy transformation are now common goals shared by nations. Taiwan has demonstrated strong 
commitment to achieving net-zero by beginning carbon accounting in 2025 and implementing carbon fees in 2026, initially targeting high-emission manufacturers and gradually extending them to the 
service sector, with rates set to increase over time. Additionally, the Executive TWD has released its Energy Transition Plan, aiming to raise the share of renewable energy to 30% and natural gas to 50% by 
2030, thus reducing reliance on coal. High electricity-consumption enterprises are now required to install or purchase green electricity or build energy storage systems. Consequently, demand for green 
power will continue to rise, along with energy costs. Taiwan's policy direction toward a low-carbon economy is now clear, and both manufacturing and service industries must proactively plan adaptive 
strategies.
While green and low-carbon products present enormous business opportunities, companies must invest considerable resources to meet carbon 
reduction targets and demonstrate a combination of transformation commitment, technical capabilities, and sufficient investment capacity. Starting 
in 2025, Everest Textile will allocate internal carbon cost provisions monthly to align with upcoming carbon fee policies and has applied for voluntary 
GHG reduction programs to obtain preferential carbon rates. Rooted in Taiwan and expanding globally, Everest has established manufacturing bases in 
Southeast Asia, China, Africa, and the United States, offering multi-functional, sustainable, and innovative products. Amid an increasingly volatile global 
operating environment, Everest recognizes the need to strengthen three core competencies: foresight, adaptability, and resilience. Foresight enables 
us to anticipate industry trends and seize early market opportunities; adaptability allows us to adjust strategies swiftly in response to changes and stay 
ahead of competitors; and resilience equips us to absorb shocks and recover faster than others.
By leveraging these capabilities—together with flexible global supply chain management and a robust product portfolio—Everest maximizes the 
synergy of its transnational operations. Through technological innovation, Everest demonstrates its ongoing commitment to environmental protection, 
social responsibility, and corporate governance. We are fully aligned with international sustainability trends, actively embracing ESG (Environmental, 
Social, and Governance) principles and integrating the spirit of the United Nations Sustainable Development Goals (UN SDGs) into our core operations 
and strategic planning to ensure stable growth in a globally competitive environment.
Everest has set concrete actions aligned with the Far Eastern Group’s “3×50” goals: a 50% reduction in carbon emissions, a 50% green product 
share, and a 50% green material share by 2030. Beyond establishing a roadmap toward net-zero emissions by 2050, we are implementing a proactive 
and clear transformation strategy, covering all aspects of the production process—from energy and raw materials to wastewater management. We are 
embedding the concepts of the circular economy and green procurement into our daily operations, from ecological design and raw material sourcing to 
finished product delivery, integrating the green supply chain and investing in low-carbon energy solutions. To increase the proportion of green products, 
Everest has launched new developments targeting low-carbon applications, including bio-based and recycled materials, water-based coatings, mono-
material lamination, and specialty composite printing—all of which combine eco-friendly resources with Everest’s core capabilities. In addition, we are 
actively developing localized low-carbon supply chains to further reduce product carbon footprints.
Everest also places great emphasis on talent development, striving to build a healthy, empowering work environment with comprehensive incentive 
systems to enhance employee professionalism and overall competitiveness. In addition to technical skill training, Everest promotes AI and digital 
upskilling, strengthening its digital capabilities to stay ahead in the wave of digital transformation. We encourage intergenerational collaboration, where 
experienced employees and younger generations work together, blending wisdom and creativity to generate new value for the company.
Upholding the spirit of Diligence, Sincerity, Simplicity, Prudence, and Innovation, Everest integrates ecological design, green manufacturing 
technologies, and climate adaptation into its operational strategies. In recognition of our sustainability achievements, Everest was honored with multiple 
prestigious awards in 2024, including: 
Bronze Award – National Enterprise Environmental Protection Award
Gold Award – TCSA Taiwan Corporate Sustainability Report Award (Traditional Manufacturing) TCSA Corporate Sustainability Excellence Award
Water Resource Leadership Award – TCSA Single Performance
Silver Award – TSAA Taiwan Sustainability Action Award (Circular Economy)
ASSET Sustainability Model Award – Social Enterprise Sustainability
These accolades affirm Everest’s outstanding ESG performance and further establish our position as a preferred supplier to leading global brands. I 
sincerely thank all our colleagues, customers, shareholders, and stakeholders for your trust and support. We look forward to continuing to work hand-in-
hand with partners across all sectors to foster innovation, strive for excellence, and build a strong foundation for Everest Textile’s sustainable growth.
Chairman of Everest Textile
Co.,Ltd. Jonny Hih

Everest announced that it will move towards net-zero carbon 
emissions by 2050 and create a low-carbon future with three 
major strategies
1.Strategies to reduce carbon emissions in response to climate
change    SDGs 7.2
In the face of extreme climate challenges, Everest has implemented a number 
of carbon reduction measures, from production processes to building energy 
conservation and low-carbon product design, to comprehensively promote 
energy conservation and emission reduction.
0.5 Sustainability Topics
0.5 Sustainability Topics
SDGs 7.2
Net Zero Commitments
Short-, Medium-, and Long-Term Targets
With 2020 as the base year, we will promote three major carbon reduction 
strategies to move towards net zero:
Strategy 1: Equipment upgrades and green energy deployment
Strategy 2: Equipment replacement and energy efficiency improvement
Strategy 3: Process optimization and Wisdom Everest system
Reduce carbon emissions by 25% by 2025
Reduce carbon emissions by 50% by 2030 
Achieve net-zero emissions by 2050
【Building a Solar Power Generation System】
【Carbon Reduction Measures in the Manufacturing Process】 
Everest's main emission source is the boiler. Currently, clean coal technology 
has been adopted to increase boiler efficiency and reduce fuel consumption, and 
a portion of biomass fuel is used to replace coal. In 2025, Everest plans to switch 
boiler fuel to natural gas (LNG) as the primary source. The initial investment 
cost for the natural gas pipeline installation is 9.8 million TWD, and the cost for 
replacing the fuel oil boiler combustion chamber is 6.29 million TWD. Based 
on the 2021 boiler fuel consumption, full conversion to LNG can reduce 38,988 
tCO2e/year.
Regarding equipment upgrades, 
Everest will eliminate outdated machinery 
and implement automation process 
management in 2024, reducing carbon 
emissions by approximately 4,153 tCO2e/
year
Remarks: Please refer to the content of this ESG Report for relevant data referenced in the 
Annual Report
In accordance with the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) set by 
the United Nations, Everest is transitioning to low-carbon production, 
investing in new energy, energy conservation and carbon reduction 
strategies, actively responding to the climate and environmental crisis 
caused by global warming, fulfilling corporate responsibilities to the 
environment and society, and actively moving towards the goal of 
net-zero carbon emissions by 2025. (Low-carbon/renewable energy 
transition.)
Everest’s Taiwan Plant plans to self-generate and use solar power to reduce 
purchased electricity, constructing the third and fourth phases of its solar power 
generation systems. The total investment is 15,578 million TWD, with completion 
expected in July 2024. The first and second 
phases are leased to operators. The estimated 
power generation of the third phase is 
1,228,470 kWh/year (capacity: 1,008 kW). The 
estimated power generation of the fourth 
phase is 3,751,871 kWh/year (capacity: 3,088 
kW). The total estimated reduction in carbon 
emissions from the third and fourth phases is 
2,460 tons/year.

2.Sustainable development and green product research &
development
Everest is well aware of the importance of sustainable development, with 
sustainability and innovation at its core, and has developed a variety of green 
products to respond to market demand and environmental protection trends.
【Cross-border cooperative development】
0.5 Sustainability Topics
【Raw Material Procurement and Product Design】
3.Cross-border cooperation opportunities brought about by the
sports trend
 In recent years, the rise of sports culture has led to an increasing demand 
for functionality and fashion, creating value-added opportunities for the textile 
industry. Through cross-border cooperation with diverse industries, Everest has 
successfully expanded the application scope of its products and added new value 
to the brand.
In terms of raw material selection, Everest gives priority 
to materials that meet environmental standards such 
as "recyclable", "renewable" and "biodegradable", and 
cooperates with suppliers to ensure the use of dyes and 
additives that meet the BLUESIGN® STANDARD, reducing 
negative environmental impacts. In product design, Everest 
emphasizes sustainability and environmental protection 
by using organic cotton, recycled fibers, and other eco-
friendly materials. It has also developed degradable 
and biodegradable PET & cotton blends to reduce non-
degradable waste.
【Green Supply Chain and Social Responsibility】
Everest strengthens cooperation with local suppliers, promotes green supply 
【New Product Development】
Everest actively promotes the circular economy, and has developed new 
products such as PET bottle recycling film, single material lamination, and water-
based coating lamination. These products have been widely recognized in the 
market and have won multiple awards at Germany’s ISPO Outdoor Products 
Exhibition. With its innovative RE:NEO next-generation screen protection cape, 
Everest stood out at the 2025 iF Design Award, demonstrating its outstanding 
strength in sustainable textiles and high-performance design.
【Fusion of fashion and sports】
Everest cooperates with trendy brands to develop clothing that combines 
both fashion appeal and sports functionality. These garments feature unique 
print effects and incorporate moisture absorption, antibacterial and anti-odor, 
and UV protection functions. This not only attracts fashion enthusiasts but also 
enhances the brand’s added value and market visibility.
【Promoting sustainable development】
Everest actively responds to the environmental movement by partnering 
with environmental organizations to develop eco-friendly sportswear made 
from renewable or recycled materials. It applies single-material design to create 
multi-functional products, expanding market reach and addressing consumer 
needs for variety and innovation. In addition, Everest combines designer fashion 
elements with the technical advantages of the textile industry, maintaining 
product functionality and comfort while enhancing its fashion value.

Everest cooperated with BASF, a major chemical 
manufacturer, to develop a tire-recycled woven 
elastic fabric, which was favored by a well-known 
German racing sponsor brand. The plan involves 
handing over recycled racing tires to BASF for

In 2024, Everest was honored to be invited to participate in the 'Nanbowan No.1 - Spotlight Tainan' exhibition. The company has 
a vertically integrated and streamlined production process, focusing on innovation and sustainable development. The company 
promotes the concepts of "clothing safety" and "healthy wear", and is dedicated to developing textile products that are friendly to 
both humans and the environment. Rooted in Tainan, Everest connects local resources with the global market, and through a dual 
R&D system, rapidly launches new products to enhance market competitiveness. The company actively promotes ESG practices, 
using eco-friendly materials to develop innovative fabrics. Everest will continue to lead the industry and become a global leader in 
low-carbon and intelligent textiles.
Inside the Nanbowan Theater, the surrounding black fabric was supplied by the company, made from recycled PET bottles, with 
a high-quality texture.

【AI-Powered Fabric Quality Inspection】
In traditional manufacturing processes, after fabric samples are produced, 
quality assurance personnel need to manually inspect the fabric and record any 
defects. This not only consumes a lot of manpower but also risks missing defects 
due to visual fatigue, leading to potential customer complaints. Everest has 
introduced the EVS intelligent fabric inspection system from Israel, which uses 
high-speed cameras to perform AOI (Automated Optical Inspection) of the fabric 
surface, locate defect positions, and then move a spectrophotometer left and 
right to analyze color differences. This not only reduces labor requirements, but 
also increases productivity by 30%
【Smart Membrane Production System】
Everest has collaborated with the Industrial Technology Research Institute and 
Advantech to integrate AI (Artificial Intelligence) and IoT (Internet of Things), 
developing a proprietary AIOT (Artificial Intelligence of Things) system for its 
waterproof and breathable membrane production process. This system uses 
sensors to monitor the production parameters of the waterproof and breathable 
membranes online, and establishes a production history traceability system to 
ensure product quality. The key advantage is the application of AI's deep learning 
capabilities to the membrane production equipment, training cloud-based 
machines to make intelligent judgments and generate data-driven insights. This 
achieves the goal of integrating smart technology with the textile industry.

0.5 Sustainability Topics
4. Intelligent transformation in the AI era
Since the end of 2024, Everest has been committed to promoting digital
transformation and has successively added the following intelligent automation 
equipment to reduce manual workload.
【Automated Dyeing Chemical Dosing】
Everest has introduced the ENMOS automatic chemical weighing system from 
Turkey and the automatic auxiliary agent weighing system from Liuya, integrating 
the control systems of different models of dyeing machines and connecting 
them to the MES (Manufacturing Execution System). After the operator scans 
the process card barcode to weigh chemicals, the fabric is fed into the dyeing 
machine, and the machine control system automatically calls the MES system, 
transmitting the chemical weighing data and machine parameter information 
to the central control system for subsequent automatic chemical weighing and 
dyeing operations.
In July 2024, Everest shared its plan to use a 
5G dedicated frequency and private network 
to implement an intelligent factory logistics 
AGV system. This will effectively reduce manual 
labor, excess mileage, and energy consumption, 
set a benchmark for manufacturing logistics, 
and support Everest's goal of achieving carbon 
neutrality by 2050.
5. Everest Textile Eco-Industrial Park
To reduce manufacturing costs and implement the concept of an eco-friendly enterprise,
Everest has actively promoted green buildings and environmental sustainability. It uses 
climbing plants as green curtains, which block radiant heat while introducing cool air, 
improving office comfort. At the same time, four ecological ponds have been set up, where 
water evaporation carries away heat, and aquatic plants are planted to absorb carbon, 
effectively reducing carbon emissions and mitigating the heat island effect.
【Ecological Greening Project】 Circular Economy Reduces Costs and 
Creates Revenue
Everest continues to update its "Diamond-Level Renovation of Existing Buildings" Green 
Building Label from the Ministry of the Interior and the "Green Factory Label" from the 
Ministry of Economic Affairs, strengthening its green factory construction. Through these 
measures, Everest not only reduces costs, but also further enhances its environmental 
commitment, moving toward more competitive and sustainable development goals.
Taiwan Factory
Everest's Tainan factory has passed the Green Factory Cleaner Production Evaluation 
System and obtained the Green Factory Label certificate, demonstrating its continuous 
efforts and leading position in green innovation. The factory's twisting building has also 
been awarded the Diamond-Level Green Building certification, highlighting its excellent 
performance in energy efficiency, resource management, and environmental design. These 
achievements demonstrate Everest's commitment to environmental protection and social 
responsibility while pursuing economic benefits, setting a good example for the industry.
Thailand Factory
In 2017, Everest's factory in Thailand received the first overseas version of Taiwan's 
green building certification for "Old Building Improvement - Diamond Level," marking a 
successful step for Taiwan's green building assessment system into the international market. 
In 2023, Everest's Thailand factory once again obtained the Diamond-Level Green Building 
certification, further solidifying its leading position in the fields of environmental protection 
and sustainable development. These achievements demonstrate Everest's relentless efforts 
and outstanding performance in promoting green innovation and sustainable building 
globally.
【Natural Negative Pressure Principle】
Since 2008, Everest has required its three factories - the Taiwan plant, the Thailand plant, 
and the Shanghai plant - to turn off air conditioning and use water curtains, mist systems, or 
plant-based green curtains to block the infiltration of external hot air into the factory. Exhaust 
fans are also used to expel heat generated by the machinery inside the factory.
At the same time, due to the negative pressure effect, fresh air from outside is drawn into 
the factory. As the air passes through the water curtain, water evaporation carries away the 
heat, maintaining factory temperatures between 28 ° C and 30 ° C. This approach has also 
earned Everest the highest-level Diamond Green Building certification for its old building 
renovation.

0.6 Everest Sustainable Development Model
0.6 Everest Sustainable Development Model
GRI 2-13
Global warming is an increasingly serious issue, and enterprises must shoulder 
social responsibilities to promote sustainable development. As early as April 2007, 
Everest launched the "Everest Sustain-Ability Model (ESM)", emphasizing the 
balanced development of the economy, society, and the environment. Internally, 
Everest actively cultivates employees' environmental awareness and promotes 
the "Energy Saving, Environmental Protection, Love the Earth" strategic actions. It 
also mobilizes the supply chain and community to jointly participate in ecological 
conservation, striving for the co-prosperity of the enterprise and the environment.
To implement the sustainable production concept of "Less is More", Everest is 
committed to improving resource use efficiency and has set a goal of zero waste 
discharge for its three factories, in order to build green competitiveness and move 
toward the vision of becoming a leader in ecological enterprise development. Facing 
the global trends of carbon neutrality and emission reduction, the company actively 
responds to international environmental protection standards by introducing 
energy-saving equipment and renewable energy to reduce its carbon footprint and 
achieve an environmentally friendly operating model.
Sustainable Development Policy
Everest's Sustainable Development Policy is formulated by the Board 
of Directors as the highest level of sustainable governance, with regular 
review and reporting of sustainability-related issues. In 2014, the "Corporate 
Social Responsibility Policy" was formulated, and in 2022 it was revised to 
the "Corporate Sustainability Development Policy" in accordance with the 
"Sustainable Development Best Practice Principles for TWSE/GTSM Listed 
Companies" and approved by the Board of Directors for implementation.
Everest, as Taiwan's only vertically integrated long- and short-fiber textile 
mill, upholds the mission of "Contributing to society and transforming 
the world through innovation and sustainability", and has introduced the 
Cradle to Cradle concept to promote environmentally friendly design and 
green manufacturing processes, developing textiles that are harmless to the 
ecosystem and reducing environmental impact. At the same time, Everest 
attaches importance to human rights and workplace safety, providing 
employees with a healthy and energy-efficient work environment, and 
promoting the concept of sustainability to the community and supply chain, 
realizing the co-prosperity of the enterprise and society.
The company attaches great importance to stakeholder participation 
and feedback, with diverse communication mechanisms such as employee 
opinion forms, complaint systems, union communications, and suggestion 
boxes. For major external issues, careful review is conducted, and approval 
from management representatives and the highest management level is 
required before public disclosure. This governance framework demonstrates 
Everest's emphasis on due diligence, risk management, and engagement 
procedures, fulfilling its corporate citizenship responsibilities and moving 
towards sustainable development goals.
ESG Global Deployment Organization
In 2022, the company launched the ESG Global Deployment Organization. 
The Chairman is Chief Operating Officer Chen Yi-peng, the Vice Chairman is 
Chief Administrative Officer Li Xian-zhong, and the Sustainability Officer is Vice 
President Lin Huang-shan. They are responsible for overseeing the execution of 
ESG-related matters, integrating the Advanced Technology Research Institute 
and R&D Department, and collaborating closely with the EHS, marketing, utilities, 
and management departments, as well as external advisory consultants. This 
aims to continuously deepen the formulation and promotion of the company’s 
overall sustainable management strategy.
Progress is reported to the Board of Directors quarterly, and annual ESG 
implementation results are reported to senior management. This gradually 
embeds ESG as a core value of the company. There are four subgroups under this 
organization: Environmental Protection (E), Social Responsibility (S), Corporate 
Governance (G), and the Overseas Plant Group.
The greenhouse gas inventory progress at global operating sites is reported 
at the annual Board of Directors meeting. In addition, the RO water recycling 
capital expenditure case was reported on November 9, 2023, and the Corporate 
Sustainability Report (ESG Report) and stakeholder communication were 
presented on August 6, 2024.

0. Introduction
1. Company Vision
2. Vision and
     leadership
3.The rise of
green energy
4. Social Sustainable 
Development
Appendix
Everest fulfills its corporate social responsibility (CSR) and 
embeds the spirit of corporate citizenship into its business 
decisions, implementing the following strat
Promotion:The company commits to expanding its social responsibility 
to all operational levels, and promotes the requirement for suppliers and 
subcontractors to comply with relevant requirements, ensuring that all business 
interactions and public welfare activities strive to fulfill social responsibility.
Management System:The company commits to complying with labor 
standards and environmental, health, and safety related regulations, and through 
the operation of the management system and PDCA continuous improvement, 
forms a complete and practical management mechanism.
Employees:The company practices humane treatment, encourages 
employees to communicate and exchange with senior management, provides 
employment opportunities for the physically and mentally disabled, implements 
environmental health and safety management, provides employees with energy-
efficient and environmentally friendly safe working environments, and cultivates 
healthy living habits, so that employees take pride in the company.
Health and Safety:The company is committed to industrial waste reduction, 
energy saving, resource recycling, and zero-disaster initiatives, and properly 
monitors substances that may pose risks to the environment and employee 
health and safety at every stage.
Environment:The company aims to achieve environmental sustainability 
through ecological restoration and respect for biodiversity. It has built the 
Huan-TWD Eco-Industrial Park and the Huan-TWD Natural Vegetable and Fruit 
Education Farm based on the concept of green buildings, and promotes these 
initiatives to the local community, hoping to establish the educational farm as a 
model of sustainable agriculture and to contribute to global warming mitigation.
Social:The company actively participates in community engagement and 
sponsorship activities, caring for the elderly and underprivileged groups in the 
local community. It collaborates with the local community to organize various 
arts, performances, and community ecological greening activities, in order to 
enhance the positive interaction between the company and the community.
Economy:The company adopts the Cradle to Cradle philosophy as its core 
principle, incorporating environmental design, blue manufacturing processes, 
and green products, striving to develop textile products that are harmless to 
humans and the ecosystem, thereby reducing environmental impact.
Manufacturing: Implement 5S management, dedicated to developing high-
efficiency, low-pollution, energy-saving, and high-safety manufacturing 
processes.
Responding to the United Nations Global Compact (UN Global 
Compact)
Everest actively responds to the United Nations Global Compact (UN Global 
Compact), supporting its 10 universal principles covering the four areas of human 
rights, labor, environment, and anti-corruption. The Compact calls on companies 
to play a key role in promoting sustainable and responsible development in 
their global operations. The principles include "Businesses should ensure they 
are not complicit in human rights abuses", "Eliminate discrimination in respect 
of employment and occupation", "Encourage the development and diffusion of 
environmentally friendly technologies", and "Work against corruption in all its 
forms".
Everest has integrated these principles into its corporate governance and 
operational practices. Through the formulation of a "Social Responsibility 
Handbook" and various management regulations, the company implements its 
responsibilities in labor rights protection, environmental protection, workplace 
ethics, and fair trade.
The company continues to track international sustainability trends and ESG 
standard developments, and proactively plans education and training, as well 
as system strengthening for high-risk issues, in order to enhance organizational 
resilience and sustainable competitiveness.
In the future, Everest will deepen its commitment to the 10 UNGC principles, 
strengthen dialogue and cooperation with stakeholders, and fulfill its corporate 
citizenship responsibilities. It will actively promote a sustainable value chain, 
low-carbon transformation, and transparent governance, contributing to the 
realization of global sustainable development goals (SDGs).
0.6 Everest Sustainable Development Model
GRI 2-23、2-24
Procurement: The company is committed to selecting raw material suppliers 
that comply with green manufacturing processes and product requirements, 
integrating a green procurement supply chain to reduce its carbon footprint.
Business: The company aims to transform customer purchasing patterns, market 
green products, and collaborate with customers to develop sustainable business 
plans.

0.7 Communication with Stakeholders
0.7 Communication with Stakeholders
GRI 2-29、3
0.7.1  Identifying Stakeholders and Significant Topics
This report determines significant topics through the following 
six steps.
1. Identify stakeholders
The company's managers and above will fill out the questionnaire, score the
stakeholders that may be contacted or affected by their business, and identify 
the key stakeholders of Everest.
14 categories of stakeholders, Identify 7 categories of stakeholders
2. Summary of sustainable issues
With reference to international norms and standards (GRI General Standards
2021, SASB Sustainability Accounting Standards, SDGs, stakeholder opinions, 
TCFD identification results, etc.), review the company's operating activities and 
partnerships and analyze the list of sustainable issues in the industry, which are 
divided into three aspects: economy, environment, and society (including human 
rights), and summarize them.
Collect 62 sustainable issues, Focus on 19 sustainable issues
3.Impact of sustainable issues on the economy
Through the distribution of questionnaires, the impact of the issues of concern
to each stakeholder is measured, the questionnaires are collected, and the results 
are analyzed.The questionnaires are distributed to seven key stakeholders, 
including customers, employees, suppliers, government agencies, shareholders, 
financial institutions and NGO groups.
Questionnaires issued by relevant responsible units of the company,Collect 183 
questionnaires
4.Impact of sustainable issues on company operations
The company's managers and above will fill out the questionnaire, the degree
and incidence of positive and negative impacts of each issue will be measured, 
the impact of each issue on Everest's operations will be identified and scored, 
and the results will be analyzed.
Distributed to relevant responsible supervisors in three major aspects, Collect 36 
impact questionnaires
5.Ranking of major topics
The degree and incidence of positive and negative impacts are counted, and a
positive and negative impact matrix is drawn. The positive and negative impacts 
and the degree of stakeholder concern are integrated to calculate the overall 
significance and ranking.
Draw a matrixEvaluate positive and negative impacts, Ranking of major themes 
in 2024
6.Review and analysis of results
The company analyzes the ranking results internally and selects 7 major
themes based on the average value, which are approved by the ESG Global 
Promotion Organization. Everest will continue to strengthen management and 
disclose relevant information in the sustainability report.
Confirmed by senior management, 7 major themes
Stakeholder Identification Results
Everest uses the AA1000 SES stakeholder consultation standard, applying 
five principles: dependence, responsibility, influence, multiple perspectives, and 
attention tension, to identify and rank stakeholders.

Positive and negative impacts of sustainable issues in 2024
Everest uses its own sustainable actions to assess the positive and negative 
impacts on the economy, environment, and society (including human rights), and 
the likelihood of occurrence, draws positive and negative impact severity charts, 
and identifies the "highly positive impact opportunities" and "highly negative 
impact risks" the company is currently facing. For highly positive impact issues, 
the company will continue to plan to expand and deepen their influence; it will 
actively manage highly negative impact issues, formulate response policies, and 
reduce the severity and probability of negative impacts.
Matrix of major topics in 2024
In order to make it easier for stakeholders to assess the impact of sustainable 
development issues, the company updated the names of sustainable 
development issues in 2024 and adopted the "double materiality" concept 
proposed by the Global Reporting Initiative (GRI) and supported by the 
European Union, identifying 7 major topics that have a high impact on company 
operations, as well as on the economy, environment, and people (including 
human rights).

0.7.2 Major topic scope and boundaries
Explanation of major topic changes in 2024:
Cause of Change :
Integration of sustainable issues
Description of changes:
In order to strengthen management effectiveness and avoid duplication, "Environmental Sustainability Policy" and "Pollution Prevention" are integrated into "Climate 
Change and Environmental Protection" and "Waste Management", and the environmental protection aspect is expanded in accordance with the TCFD strategy to 
systematically respond to climate risks. "Responding to Climate Change" is renamed to "Climate Change and Environmental Protection", integrating climate and 
environmental strategies to strengthen risk response. "Low-carbon Energy Transformation" is subdivided into "Energy Management" and "Low-carbon/Renewable Energy 
Transformation", and the sub-items are helpful for strategic resource allocation and progress tracking. "Employee Training and Welfare" focuses on career development, 
strengthens health promotion and welfare systems, and improves talent retention and productivity. "Recruitment Diversity and Inclusion" implements an equal workplace, 
increases the participation of women and vulnerable groups, and promotes diversified innovation. "Happy Workplace" has been removed to focus on core projects, 
because its related content has been covered in the newly added social issues.
Cause of Change:
Major theme adjustments
Description of changes:
Based on the results of the double materiality analysis, "operating performance" and "innovative green products" will be added in 2024 to align with financial disclosure 
practices and the sustainability of green products. "Integrity management" will be deleted.

0.7.3 Major Theme Management Policy
0.7 Communication with Stakeholders
GRI 2-29
Major topic: Operating performance  GRI 3-3
Management Policy and Commitment
With stable operation and sustainable development as the core, Everest continues to optimize its operating strategy, strengthen the company's foundation, consolidate its 
industry leadership, and drive industry upgrading. The company has established an effective internal control and risk management framework through a sound corporate 
governance system and integrity management mechanism, has identified key risks that affect operating performance, and responded immediately to avoid financial 
losses and goodwill risks.
Through regular business review meetings and quarterly board meetings, we ensure that the operating direction and strategy are continuously optimized.
Everest attaches great importance to organizational culture and values. Employees take integrity, altruism, and daily improvement as their code of conduct, creating long-
term corporate value through integrity and responsibility, and achieve the dual goals of stable growth and shareholder returns.
Tracking mechanism (responsible unit)
The ESG Global Implementation Organization's Corporate Governance Group regularly meets with executives to review its progress.
Resources and management mechanisms
• The "Rules of Procedure for Board Meetings" stipulate the avoidance of conflicts of interest. If there is a donation from a related party or a major donation to a non-
related party, it should be reported to the board of directors, and violations of ethical behavior and integrity management should be punished.
• The "Risk Management System for Preventing Terrorism and Economic Sanctions" stipulates a plan to prevent money laundering.
• Anti-bribery clauses are clearly stipulated in the procurement contract.
• The board of directors tracks the goals every quarter and strengthens the risk warning mechanism.
【2025 發展目標】
Management Actions
2024 Target :
Develop green, environmentally friendly, and 
low-carbon process products to increase green 
product revenue.
2025 Target :
• Develop green and low-carbon process products
and increase green product revenue.
• The ratio of people receiving integrity and ethics
training reached 95%.
• No records of corruption or major integrity
violations.
2030 Target :
• Steadily improve annual revenue and profit performance
to achieve mid- and long-term financial goals.
• Expand green products and emerging market presence to
create new growth momentum in the future.
• Strengthen risk warning and response mechanisms to
reduce financial and operational disruption risks.
2024 Performance
• 1,364 people received integrity and morality, with no corruption incidents in 2024.
• All new employees have completed information security education and training, and there were zero cybersecurity incidents.
Effectiveness evaluation and tracking
• Business review meetings are held regularly to track business performance and require related units to improve.
• Board meetings are held quarterly to ensure continuity and appropriateness of strategic direction.
• Regularly communicate financial performance and development strategies to shareholders and investors.

0.7 Communication with Stakeholders
GRI 2-29
Major theme: Partnership management  GRI 3-3
Management Policy and Commitment
Everest sees partnership management as the key to improving competitiveness and profitability. Through the information management system, customer data and 
transaction records are integrated, and customized services are provided based on the classification mechanism and satisfaction survey results to reduce churn and 
strengthen brand trust. The company regularly participates in domestic and international exhibitions, holds customer talks and satisfaction surveys, and continuously 
optimizes the product and service experience. In order to strengthen the stability of the supply chain, Everest has established procurement platforms in various locations, 
partnered with regional suppliers to promote digital supply networks and green procurement, and established a long-term cooperation mechanism. Suppliers are also 
required to sign social responsibility guidelines, and their performance in terms of environment, labor, and human rights is monitored through visits, meetings, and 
evaluations, to jointly build a resilient and sustainable value chain.
Tracking mechanism (responsible unit)
The Business Department and the Sales and Production Department regularly communicate with customers and strictly protect customer information.
Resources and management mechanisms
• Establish an information-based customer management system to integrate basic information, transaction records and demand preferences.
• Regularly participate in domestic and international exhibitions and hold customer meetings to enhance brand visibility and customer relationships.
• Conduct annual customer satisfaction surveys to continuously optimize the product and service experience.
• Implement customer data protection and promote the development of safe and green raw materials to respond to sustainable needs.

GRI 2-29
Major theme: Innovative green products  GRI 3-3
Management Policy and Commitment
Everest is committed to innovative R&D and green product development, promoting the application of low-carbon, non-toxic, and recyclable materials to achieve the 
sustainability goal of economic and environmental integration. In response to the global trend of green transformation, it continues to focus on R&D innovation, vertical 
integration, and local supply chain layout, and develops products with energy efficiency and carbon reduction benefits through strategies such as single-material design, 
carbon capture technology, and the introduction of biomass materials. Everest promises to achieve environmentally sustainable innovation goals by 2030, promote the 
circular economy and Textile-to-Textile (T2T) applications, enhance brand competitiveness and market influence, and contribute substantial actions to a low-carbon future.
Tracking mechanism (responsible unit)
The Advanced Technology Research Institute and the Development Liaison Department continuously confirm the status of product development.
Resources and management mechanisms
• It has a research and development unit called the [Advanced Technology Research Institute] that is distinct from other textile companies and can independently develop
new green products.
• The Taiwan factory is a textile factory that can integrate resources to design and develop new green products starting from the initial yarn.
• Cooperates with Southern Taiwan University of Science and Technology, the Textile Technology Research Institute, and the Industrial Technology Research Institute.

recycled materials.

environmental protection.

by 2030, with more than 80% of functional products to
achieve efficient product recycling and reuse.

materials will grow by 28% in 2024 compared with 2023.

0.7 Communication with Stakeholders
GRI 2-29
Major theme: Low-carbon/renewable energy transition  GRI 3-3
Management Policy and Commitment
Everest regards climate change and resource challenges as the key to sustainable development, actively promotes low-carbon and renewable energy transformation, 
introduces the TCFD framework to grasp climate risks and opportunities, and implements three major climate response strategies. Through process optimization, solar 
energy introduction, boiler conversion to natural gas, energy management system (ISO 50001) and other actions to improve energy efficiency and reduce greenhouse gas 
emissions.
Annual greenhouse gas inventory is carried out to clarify the priority of reduction. At the same time, water resources, waste and air pollution management are 
strengthened, water conservation and recycling and non-toxic chemical control are implemented, green parks and office spaces are built, and regulatory compliance and 
environmental protection go hand in hand to demonstrate low-carbon and sustainable commitments.
Tracking mechanism (responsible unit)
The Climate & Environmental Protection Group of the ESG Global Implementation Organization holds regular sustainability meetings to discuss and confirm the 
achievement of various goals.
Resources and management mechanisms
Everest introduced the TCFD climate risk assessment framework, formulated three major carbon reduction strategies (equipment renewal and green energy layout, 
equipment replacement and energy efficiency improvement, process management and smart factories), and integrated them with the ISO50001 energy management 
system to promote improvement. Through the conversion of boilers to low-carbon fuels, the introduction of renewable energy, the optimization of water recycling 
systems and the source management of chemicals, carbon reduction, and resource management capabilities are comprehensively strengthened. At the same time, 
through education and training, the energy conservation, carbon reduction and water conservation awareness of all employees are strengthened to create a green 
operation system.
Management Actions
2024 Target :
• Reduce carbon emissions by 20%.
• Reduce energy consumption by 6%.
• Equipment replacement and process improvement 
reduce CO2e emissions by 1,000t.
• The fourth phase of solar energy was completed.
2025 Target :
•  Reduce carbon emissions by 25%.
•  Reduce energy consumption by 7%.
•  Reduce energy consumption by 5,000GJ by replacing 
equipment and improving processes.
•  Set up a self-generated solar power generation system 
and plan to replace boiler fuel with natural gas (LNG).
2030 Target :
•  Reduce energy consumption by 12% by 2030.
•  Reduce carbon emissions by 50% by 2030 and 
reach net zero carbon emissions by 2050.
•  Reduce energy consumption by 5,000GJ through 
equipment replacement and process improvement.
•  Renewable energy accounts for 20% of the 
world's four plants.
2024 Performance
•  The fourth phase of solar energy construction was completed, equipment replacement and process improvement reduced emissions 
by 4,153 tCO2e.
•  Compared with the base year 2020, greenhouse gas emissions were 97,011 tCO2e, a decrease of 22.58%, achieving the established 
target.
•  Compared with the base year 2020, energy intensity was 82.75GJ/T, a decrease of 23.43%, achieving the established target.
Effectiveness evaluation and tracking
With 2020 as the base year, Everest has set medium- and long-term goals for low-carbon transformation, water resources and pollution 
prevention, and reviews the progress of carbon reduction and energy efficiency improvement through biweekly three-plant meetings. 
It tracks water use and recycling rates every month, gradually increases the utilization rate of recycled water, and regularly monitors 
air pollution and waste emissions, spot checks the compliance of chemical use, and continuously improves to achieve net zero and 
environmental sustainability goals.

GRI 2-29
Major theme: Labor Rights Protection  GRI 3-3
Management Policy and Commitment
Everest attaches great importance to human rights protection and promises to follow international standards such as the United Nations Universal Declaration of Human 
Rights and the International Labor Organization Tripartite Declaration of Principles, formulates human rights policies and regularly conducts human rights due diligence. 
The company prevented discrimination, child labor and forced labor throughout operations, assessed the current status of human rights management in 2023, and 
optimized the complaint and remedy mechanism.
The company introduced the SLCP social labor integration project and completed 5 factory audits in 2024, covering working hours, accommodation, interviews and 
other aspects. Through ISO 45001 and other certifications, the company strengthens occupational safety and labor-management communication, implements equal pay, 
working conditions and promotion opportunities, continuously improves labor conditions and employee welfare, and demonstrates the company's respect and protection 
of human rights.
Tracking mechanism (responsible unit)
The Social Responsibility Group (Human Resources Department) of the ESG Global Deployment Organization regularly organizes relevant training and promotions and 
verifies the achievement of results.
Resources and management mechanisms
• Everest regularly implements human rights due diligence and early warning mechanisms, identifies major risks and establishes complaint and remediation processes.
• Introduced SLCP social labor integration projects, covering working hours, remuneration, accommodation, health and safety and other areas.
• Combined with ISO 45001 occupational health and safety and ISO 14001 environmental management systems, the company improves management mechanisms and 
strengthens monitoring and response capabilities for employee and supply chain human rights issues.
Management Actions
2024 Target :
• Zero human rights violations occurred.
• Human rights education and training is 
held regularly.
2025 Target :
• Establish a standard operating procedure for human 
rights due diligence in the supply chain, and achieve at 
least 80% of key suppliers completing human rights risk 
identification and improvement tracking.
• Employee satisfaction survey increases to over 85%.

•Achieve zero human rights violation record (including 
supply chain).
• Continue to promote a non-discriminatory and equal 
working environment, and increase the proportion of 
women and disadvantaged groups in management 
positions to more than 30%.
2024 Performance
• A total of 1,351 people participated in Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR) human rights education and training.
• 1.76% of persons with disabilities were employed in Taiwan factories, exceeding the legal ratio by 1%.
• 35 migrant workers were promoted through the plan to retain and promote mid-level technical personnel.
• 34% of supervisors in Taiwan factories are female, and 50.4% of employees are female.
Effectiveness evaluation and tracking
In 2023, Everest commissioned an inventory of the company's human rights management status and provided recommendations for 
potential risk adjustments. In 2024, five factory labor audits were completed, and all audit results met standards, covering dormitories, 
meals, working hours, and employee interviews. The company regularly monitors regulatory changes and international human rights 
standards every year to ensure that human rights policies and practices evolve accordingly, enhances the human rights awareness of 
employees and management through education and training, and promotes a workplace culture of protection and respect.

Management Policy and Commitment
Everest Industrial is committed to cultivating talent and protecting employee welfare, which is regarded as the key to the sustainable development of the enterprise.

promotion. Everest also emphasizes career development and generational succession, and promotes reserve cadre training and internship programs in cooperation with 
colleges and universities. In terms of welfare, it provides a retirement system, childcare leave, health insurance, travel activities, and employee care to strengthen work-life 
balance.
The company allocates pensions in accordance with laws and regulations, adjusts manpower, and introduces Industry 4.0 technologies in conjunction with regulatory 
changes to ensure labor rights and promote the common growth of employees and enterprises.

0.7 Communication with Stakeholders
GRI 2-29
Major theme: Occupational safety and health  GRI 3-3
Management Policy and Commitment
Everest Company firmly believes that employee health is the cornerstone of corporate sustainability and is committed to creating a safe, healthy, and zero-disaster 
workplace environment. Taiwan, Shanghai, and Thailand promote occupational safety systems based on the ISO 45001 occupational safety and health management 
system. In-plant health management in the United States is carried out in accordance with relevant OSHA regulations. Safety and health committees meet regularly 
to implement risk assessments and improvement measures to strengthen the effectiveness of occupational injury prevention. At the same time, regular health checks, 
factory medical consultations, equipment inspections, and chemical management are implemented to improve operational safety. For contractors, pre-entry briefings 
and equipment inspections are carried out to ensure construction safety and compliance. Through system improvements and instant reporting mechanisms, the PDCA 
improvement cycle is implemented to reduce the occurrence of occupational diseases and work-related injuries.
Occupational safety management not only demonstrates the company's responsibility to its employees, but also strengthens the sustainability of the supply chain and 
brand reputation, laying the foundation for operational resilience and social value
Tracking mechanism (responsible unit)
The ESG Global Implementation Organization's Social Responsibility Team (Human Resources Department, Environmental and Safety Office) regularly organizes relevant 
training and promotions and confirms the achievement status.
Resources and management mechanisms
• The factory conducts internal audits and annual external verifications in accordance with the ISO 45001 system and relevant regulations of various countries to
continuously review the effectiveness of occupational safety management.
• The Occupational Safety and Health Committee meets quarterly to track the improvement of the working environment, the handling of disaster incidents, and the
implementation of education and training.
• The RCA root cause analysis and PDCA improvement cycle are established to investigate, report, and review each occupational injury incident.
• The "Contractor Management Measures" are established to implement pre-entry inspections and in-operation supervision, and strengthen external construction risk
control.
Management Actions
2024 Target :
• Annual inspections of hazardous
machinery meet standards.
• Zero occupational diseases occur.
2025 Target :
• Strengthen safety education and training for
contractors and raise the compliance rate to 100%.
• Fire and explosion prevention drills are conducted
at least once every six months.
• The number of accidents has decreased by 20%
each year.
2030 Target :
• The goal of zero major workplace accidents is achieved.
• A health support network is established in cooperation with
local medical institutions.
• Occupational health is incorporated into the ESG health
risk governance framework to comprehensively improve
operational resilience.
2024 Performance
• A total of 247 hazardous machines were inspected and all met the standards, with no occupational disease incidents occurring.
Effectiveness evaluation and tracking
• In 2024, a total of 16 occupational injuries occurred in the Taiwan plant (including 8 off-site traffic accidents), and all have been
addressed and tracked.
• There was no occupational disease reported in 2024 (covering Taiwan, Shanghai, Thailand, and the United States).
• Fire and toxic disaster drills: Taiwan plant conducted 3 drills with 837 participants; Shanghai plant and the United States plant
conducted 2 drills each, with a total of 398 and 260 participants, respectively.
• Further traffic safety education and defensive driving concepts were implemented to reduce the risk of off-site traffic accidents.

Appendix
Stakeholder Suggestion and Communication Mechanism
Everest Industrial Group attaches great importance to communication 
and interaction with stakeholders, and has established a diversified opinion 
collection and response mechanism to facilitate the immediate grasp of all 
parties' suggestions and concerns as a basis for sustainable decision-making and 
policy adjustments. In addition to the existing complaint channels, the company 
has also set up a number of non-complaint suggestion and communication 
mechanisms, including: employee suggestion boxes and employee opinion 
forms, regularly held union meetings and safety and health committees, 
management review meetings (convened by the Board of Directors  together 
with senior executives and employee representatives to summarize the results 
of stakeholder communication as a basis for policy revisions and action plans), 
and feedback mechanisms in education and training and internal promotion 
activities.
The above mechanisms can also be integrated with the complaint system. 
If the content reflected by stakeholders through the complaint form are 
improvement suggestions or feedback, the management representative or 
relevant responsible unit will classify and handle it according to the nature of the 
content, and include it in the stakeholder consultation and follow-up tracking 
mechanism to ensure that each opinion receives appropriate attention and 
response. Everest Industrial Group effectively promotes stakeholder participation 
and implements corporate responsibility and sustainable governance through an 
institutionalized, multi-faceted and traceable communication mechanism.
Complaints Policy
Everest Industrial Group upholds the core value of honest management, 
implements honesty principles through various management regulations, 
strictly prohibits any violation of human rights, morality or integrity, and strives 
to prevent such incidents from happening within the company. Whether it 
is an employee or an external stakeholder, any illegal activities, violations of 
the company's code of conduct, human rights policies, or behaviors that may 
harm the company's reputation can be disclosed through the whistleblowing 
mechanism, so that Everest Industrial Group can promptly identify and 
address them. Everest Industrial Group has established a complaint policy, and 
complaints can be made completely anonymously. Everest Industrial Group 
will not use any means to track down the identity of the complainant. If you 
voluntarily provide your name and contact information, it will also be kept strictly 
confidential, and ensures that you will not suffer any adverse effects due to the 
disclosure. The complaint policy established by Everest Industrial Group applies 
to all stakeholders of Everest Industrial Group.
Complaints and reporting channels
Complaints can be made verbally, in writing (complaint channel box), by 
hotline or by email

Appendix
1.1 Company Overview
1.1 Company Overview
GRI 2-1
1.1.1 Company Profile
Founded in 1988, Everest Industrial is an internationally renowned smart textile 
factory for its innovation and sustainability, offering services from yarn, fabric, 
dyeing and finishing, post-processing to garments. Everest has the advantage 
of a vertically integrated factory, from R&D, raw materials, and processes 
to products, and is committed to meeting customer needs. It is dedicated 
to developing textiles that are harmless to humans and the ecosystem, and 
promoting the concepts of "clothing safety" and "healthy wear".
Everest's core product is false-twist yarn that combines functionality and 
fashion, and is widely used in eco-innovative fabrics for sports, outdoor, and 
urban environments. In order to maintain its leading position in innovation, 
Everest took the lead in establishing the "Advanced Technology Research 
Institute", a national R&D center in the domestic textile industry, in 2003, 
transforming from a "physical textile" approach to a "chemical textile" approach. 
Every year, 3% to 4% of the company's turnover is invested in R&D and 
innovation. In line with its commitment to environmental friendliness and the 
sustainable environmental policies of international brands, Everest uses eco-
friendly materials and has expanded into developing more sustainable materials 
such as dope-dyed yarn, collagen yarn, oyster yarn, and recycled spandex yarn. 
At the same time, Everest is developing fluorine-free waterproof fabrics and 
incorporating smart production, to reduce the use of chemical agents.
In recent years, extreme climate has become a common weather pattern under 
global climate change, leading to a significant increase in demand for composite 
functional textiles. Everest's long fibers, short fibers and cutting-edge products 
provide a differentiated basis for composite functional products. Through cross-
border integrated innovation and the use of emerging material technologies, 
Everest demonstrates its strong capabilities in high-performance composite 
textiles.

Business philosophy
Everest adheres to the founding spirit of the Far Eastern Group, "Diligence, 
Sincerity, Thrift, Prudence and Innovation", and is committed to sustainable 
development. It upholds integrity in management to build long-term trust, 
values hard work, to continuously improve quality, maintains a simple culture 
by adhering to a straightforward style, practices careful management to 
ensure stable operations, and pursues continuous innovation by exploring new 
technologies and methods.
Everest actively introduces environmentally friendly design, focusing on 
the development of ecological design, blue processes, and green products. 
It is committed to the research and development of textiles that are harmless 
to both humans and the environment, reducing environmental impact and 
achieving sustainable development. At the same time, the company places 
great importance on the welfare of employees, provides an energy-saving, 
environmentally friendly, safe, and healthy working environment, cultivates 
employees' natural and healthy living habits, and promotes these concepts to the 
community, manufacturers and customers to create a healthy and sustainable 
social environment.
Not only does it reduce the negative impact on the environment during 
the production process, but it also improves the overall environmental 
awareness and public health through a series of environmental and human-
centered initiatives, demonstrating the company's commitment to ecological 
protection and social responsibility. These business philosophies reflect Everest's 
determination and sense of responsibility to become an industry benchmark.

years, and at the same time, it improves its R&D capabilities to meet market trends and needs through product innovation, process innovation, technological innovation, 
and business model innovation, becoming a comprehensive solution provider with integrated advantages in the textile industry.

Everest operating bases span three continents. With Taiwan as the global logistics center, Everest has set up factories across Asia: in Tainan, Taiwan; Shanghai, 
China; and Rajapuri, Thailand. At the same time, it has expanded across the Americas and Africa, setting up factories in the United States and Ethiopia. With major 
cities such as Taipei, Shanghai, Hong Kong, Tokyo, and New York as business and marketing bases, Everest has successfully promoted its business territory worldwide 
through this dense sales and service network. The U.S. factory vertically integrates yarn weaving and dyeing processing facilities, makes good use of regional 
incentives in various countries to expand garment factories, collaborates with the global operations of existing customers in developed countries in Europe, the 
United States and Japan, and expands into emerging global markets to lay the foundation for future sustainable operations.

Enterprise Value-Global Logistics Management EV-GLM
In order to enhance the company's value and competitiveness, Everest has 
turned innovative thinking into action by promoting the IDM (Innovation Design 
Management) business model. This approach emphasizes innovative fabric 
design, and has successfully transformed Everest from a passive supplier into a 
diversified, integrated service provider, directly cooperating with apparel brands 
and distributors. Currently, Everest is actively expanding the value chain into the 
garment market. By using high-value fabrics to develop premium apparel, the 
company is realizing the innovative design goals of GIDM (Garment Innovation 
Design Management), pushing Taiwan's textile industry toward a knowledge-
intensive, service-oriented transformation.
To support these strategic goals, Everest focuses on building two key 
capabilities: one is innovative design capability, and the other is global 
operations capability. Everest has established a global operations headquarters 
to integrate these two core strengths. In terms of information systems, it 
has connected R&D resources across three regions and introduced a textile 
collaborative design platform (PDM/CPC), enabling early involvement of both 
customers and suppliers. At the same time, it integrates value chain resources 
through a global operations management system (EV-GLM) to maximize the 
benefits of its global presence. By combining innovation with strategic global 
integration, Everest continues to drive industrial upgrades and enhance its long-
term competitiveness.
EV-GLM global logistics management system operation diagram
EV-GLM is a powerful tool for Everest to leverage the benefits of its global 
layout, enhancing the company's competitive advantage through "integrating 
demand, adjusting supply and demand, global operations, making decisions in 
Taiwan, just-in-time supply, and advantageous costs."
Industry Overview
1. Current status and development of the industry
In 2024, due to high interest rates, high inflation and China's economic
recovery that is not as expected, global terminal demand is weak and 
manufacturing activities slow down. Geopolitical instability (such as the conflict 
between Russia and Ukraine and Israel and Palestine) has exacerbated global 
economic and social uncertainty. With the recent recovery of US demand 
and brand destocking, terminal demand is expected to pick up. International 
organizations predict that global trade volume will grow in 2025. Domestically, 
employment and consumption are stable, and the subsequent development of 
the textile industry is expected to pick up.
2. The correlation between the upstream, midstream and
downstream industries
The textile industry is an essential industry for people’s livelihood. The 
upstream of the industry chain is chemical fiber manufacturing (raw materials 
come from the petrochemical industry), the midstream is the spinning and false 
twisting process of natural fibers and chemical fibers, weaving and dyeing and 
finishing, and the downstream is the textile manufacturing industry such as 
ready-made clothes, apparel, curtains, etc.
3. Product development trends and competition
The world is focusing on sustainability and carbon reduction, which have
become important criteria for apparel brands to select suppliers. Taiwan's textile 
industry is actively investing in sustainable environmental protection, functional 
applications and smart manufacturing, with a particular emphasis on "sustainable 
+ functional" products. In the face of competition, companies use innovative
technologies to develop materials that take into account both environmental
protection and functionality, and consider the diversified development of the
circular economy to expand future business opportunities.

1.3.1 Research and development status
Everest adheres to the spirit of lean development, focuses on creating MVP 
(minimum viable product), combines the advantages of popular and functional 
fabrics, and continuously upgrades innovative products. The company consists 
of a cutting-edge technology research institute and R&D department, focusing 
on the research and development of functional fibers, functional post-processing 
technology and nano-level textiles. These technical R&D drivers enable Everest 
to quickly go to market, mass produce, and realize and quickly respond to 
customer needs to enhance corporate competitiveness. Everest develops high-
performance textiles through innovative technologies, uses nanotechnology 
to ensure product performance and quality, and integrates fashion elements to 
create products that are both functional and beautiful. This strategy not only 
improves market competitiveness but also enhances the company's operating 
efficiency, achieving a dual improvement in economic benefits and innovation 
capabilities, making Everest stand out in the textile industry and become an 
industry leader.
Cumulative patent approvals
One new patent was added in 2023, and there are currently 35 valid patents in 
2024, including 24 domestic inventions, 9 new domestic patents, 1 design and 1 
foreign patent (USA). It is expected to continue to grow steadily in the future and 
maintain its leading position in the industry.

As green awareness rises, Everest will continue to strengthen its ESG sustainable development, and through setting exciting customer results, building the right 
capabilities, creating effective operating models, continuously updating key insights, and reallocating investments based on returns, the company will focus on four 
aspects: vertical integration and R&D, supply chain layout, green transformation and AI leadership, in response to rapid changes and external turbulence, as explained 
below:
【Service upgrade‧Short-chain layout】New online and offline 
experience, channel integration and re-layout
With sharp insight into the apparel market, Everest integrates online and offline 
shopping experiences, flexibly responds to market changes, and continuously 
improves consumer shopping convenience and brand influence. Through one-
stop services for fabric R&D and apparel design, it strengthens supply chain 
layout and integration, ensuring efficient coordination between production 
and sales while boosting operational stability and market competitiveness. In 
addition, Everest actively expands cross-industry cooperation and marketing 
exposure, leveraging smart technology and data analysis to accurately manage 
inventory, reduce resource waste, and optimize cost structures to meet rapidly 
evolving market demands. Amid global sustainable trends, Everest also 
accelerates green production, adopting environmentally friendly materials and 
implementing energy-saving and carbon reduction measures. With strong 
supply chain integration and innovation at its core, Everest continues to expand 
its global presence and enhance brand competitiveness on all fronts.
【AI-led enterprise transformation】Implementing technological 
innovation and application to improve operational efficiency
Everest integrates digital technologies such as IOT, CIM, MES, ERP, BI, and VI

1.3 Innovative green products 
SDGs 13
[Vertical integration‧R&D focus]Recycled and bio-based materials: 50% 
each; carbon reduction target: 50%
In the face of increasingly severe natural disasters, Everest recognizes the 
urgency of mitigating the greenhouse effect and has set a long-term goal for 
2030 to fully implement innovative environmental sustainability initiatives. In 
order to achieve a closed-loop recycling cycle for garments, Everest developed 
TPEE thermoplastic polyester elastic fiber and worked with local Taiwanese 
manufacturers to jointly develop Elastomultiester polyester composite elastic 
fiber, delivering a spandex-free mono-material solution. It has also partnered 
with Far Eastern Advanced to develop polyamide PA6,6 for airbag recycling, 
realizing cross-industry cooperation and circular economy goals. In addition, 
in order to improve the energy efficiency of dyeing and finishing processes, 
Everest and Far Eastern New Century jointly developed 98 ° C low-temperature 
dyeable modified polyester fibers, endowing the material with enhanced energy-
saving features. The company actively utilizes a wide range of biomass materials, 
including livestock waste (animal feces), kitchen waste oil, bagasse, milkfish 
scales, oyster shells, corn oil, water chestnut shell charcoal, and silver wattle 
charcoal, to reduce dependence on petrochemical products and promote the 
recycling of renewable resources.
【Green transformation‧sustainable resilience】Product upgrades to 
strengthen low-carbon competitiveness
Promoting net-zero transformation is a shared challenge for Taiwan's textile 
industry. Everest actively responds to the need for carbon reduction, focusing 
on low-carbon material applications and solvent-free technology, developing 
innovative products such as carbon capture membranes, eco-friendly biofilms 
from non-food sources, and water-based PU 
products. At the same time, Everest is committed 
to sustainable material recycling by applying 
the single-material concept to waterproof and 
breathable functional clothing. The company has 
developed rTPEE-laminated and bio-based nylon 
membrane laminated fabrics, continuing to work 
toward Textile-to-Textile (T2T) circular economy 
goals and carbon neutrality. Everest proactively 
promotes material reuse, not only giving back 
to society, but also striving to build a local green 
supply chain to reduce the carbon footprint of 
its products, achieve a low-carbon economy, and 
contribute to sustainable development.
plan of the Digital Industry Administration of the 
Ministry of Digital Development, it has jointly 
implemented the factory intelligent logistics AGV 
system with Far Eastern Group. In addition, the factory 
introduced an AR Web-based machine maintenance 
management platform this year, which adopts 
cross-platform design and cross-device integration 
methods, supplemented by big data analysis of digital 
dashboards. It enables real-time tracking of repair 
progress, significantly speeds up maintenance, and 
provides quick statistical analysis to identify the most 
common causes of machine failures. This boosts 
teamwork among machine maintenance colleagues, 
reduces downtime pressure, and minimizes production 
capacity problems caused by maintenance.

1.3 Innovative green products 
SDGs 13
Biomass Balance Woven Elastic Fabric
Biomass Balance is an innovative method used by 
BASF to convert recycled agricultural waste and animal 
manure from animal husbandry into renewable raw 
materials for the chemical industry. At the beginning 
of the production process, fossil raw materials are 
mixed with renewable raw materials from sustainable 
sources to reduce carbon dioxide emissions and save 
fossil resources. Everest’s products in cooperation 
with BASF include Biomass Balance Roica and Nylon 6.

Regenerative sustainable cotton is a type of 
cotton grown using regenerative agricultural 
practices, designed to improve soil health, increase 
biodiversity, and capture carbon. Farming methods 
using regenerative agriculture help reduce soil 
degradation, improve water retention, and reduce 
the impact of harmful chemicals on the environment. 
By promoting biodiversity, the cultivation of 
regenerative sustainable cotton can also help protect 
local ecosystems and reduce the impact of pests and 
diseases. The use of cover crops and crop rotation 
helps improve soil health and fertility. Cotton is one 
of the most widely used natural fibers in the fashion 
industry. However, there are some environmental 
issues with the production of traditional cotton, 
including the use of pesticides and fertilizers, soil 
depletion, high carbon dioxide emissions, and water 
pollution.
As consumers become more aware of the impact 
of their purchasing decisions on the environment, 
the demand for sustainable and environmentally 
friendly products continues to grow. By choosing 
regenerative recycled cotton, you can rejuvenate 
the earth instead of depleting it, and truly achieve 
sustainable results.
the natural biological world and are naturally 
renewable. Renewable materials are endless, and 
products made of biomass materials can reduce 
carbon footprints, contribute to the earth and 
environmental protection, and achieve the mission 
of sustainable operation.
