Everest Taiwan Factory's Work-Related Accidents and Work Loss 
Times
Investigation and Improvement of Work-related Accidents
Everest places great importance on occupational safety and health management. 
When a work-related accident occurs, a temporary investigation team consisting of the 
supervisor of the accident unit, occupational safety personnel and related personnel 
will be immediately established to analyze the root cause of the accident using RCA 
(root cause analysis method), and an improvement and implementation plan will be 
developed in accordance with the PDCA (plan-do-check-act) cycle to prevent similar 
accidents and reduce the risk of work-related injuries. Subsequent improvement measures 
will be submitted to the Occupational Safety and Health Committee for review, and the 
implementation will be continuously tracked and supervised to enhance the efficiency 
of accident prevention and management. For employees who spontaneously participate 
in disaster relief, notify the on-site supervisor, or evacuate the site for safety reasons, 
the company will not hold them accountable for any resulting absence, which reflects 
the people-oriented safety culture. In addition, in order to promote communication on 
occupational safety and health, the company regularly engages with employees and 
contractors through the Occupational Safety and Health Committee platform to ensure 
transparency and two-way communication of workplace safety information. For the 
contractor's construction work, the company also conducts safety and health briefings 
and on-site inspections prior to commencement of work to enhance the contractor's 
safety awareness and operation level. Everest is committed to creating a safe, healthy 
and zero-disaster working environment through continuous improvements to the safety 
management system and concrete actions.
Environmental, safety and health non-compliance and corrective 
and preventive actions
Occupational Health and Safety Training
Everest regularly conducts occupational safety and health training to enhance 
employees' safety awareness and response capabilities. The training content 
includes general safety education, specialized training (such as noise hazards, 
chemical protection, forklift operation, etc.), and  pre-construction safety 
briefings and inspections for contractors. These trainings are targeted at specific 
working environments to ensure employees can effectively respond to specific 
hazards.
The contents of education and training in each factory are as 
follows:

Occupational health and safety performance evaluation
Everest Company regularly evaluates occupational safety and health 
performance and continuously improves the management system through data 
analysis. In 2024, the injury rate of the Taiwan factory was 0.55, the Shanghai 
factory was 0.58, the Thailand factory was 0.12, and the US factory was 1.6. No 
occupational diseases occurred in the four factories. The company continues to 
track the improvement of work-related accidents through the PDCA (Plan-Do-
Check-Act) cycle.
Occupational safety and health performance statistics in 2024
【Contractor Management】
Before entering the factory for construction, contractors must complete the 
relevant pre-construction work in accordance with the factory's "Contractor 
Management Measures", fill in the "Contractor's Safety Instructions for 
Construction Work in the Factory" and the "Safety Permit Application Form", 
and submit them to the factory for review and approval before construction 
can begin. Depending on the construction method, the "Safety Checklist for 
Various Operations" must be completed before the construction day. The 
work content includes: general construction work such as hot work, elevated 
construction, trench excavation, etc. The factory supervisor must confirm the 
items in the "Safety Checklist for Various Operations" and only start construction 
after confirming that there are no abnormalities. At the Shanghai factory, when 
signing special project contracts with suppliers and contractors, both parties 
sign a "Contractor Operation Safety Agreement". Prior to the start of the project, 
a "Special Project Start-up Order" must be signed and approved. Meetings are 
organized to communicate and coordinate safety and health matters, ensure 
compliance with occupational safety laws and factory regulations, implement 
protective measures and control procedures, and maintain a safe construction 
environment.
Everest's factory conducts various safety inspections on construction work in 
accordance with the "Contractor Management Regulations" to ensure the safety 
of construction personnel, avoid work-related injuries, create a safe working 
environment, and achieve the goal of zero accidents. Emergency management 
regulations and other relevant documents have been formulated to standardize 
relevant emergency disposal processes. Fire drills are conducted every six 
months, and all drills are conducted in conjunction with external authorities. To 
ensure that contractors can work safely in the factory, contractors must register 
and renew their licenses, conduct safety publicity, check safety equipment, and 
comply with the company's safety regulations before entering the factory every 
day for construction.
Occupational Health and Safety Emergency Response
Everest Company has formulated a comprehensive emergency response 
management system and conducts regular fire drills to improve employees' 
response capabilities. In 2024, the Taiwan factory held three full-factory fire drills, 
with a total of 837 participants; the Shanghai factory and the US factory held two 
emergency escape trainings, with 398 and 260 participants respectively, ensuring 
quick and effective responses in the event of a disaster. Before entering the 
factory, contractors must conduct safety promotion and equipment inspections 
to ensure construction safety. These measures ensure that contractors comply 
with company safety regulations during construction and reduce construction 
risks.

Remarks: Calculation rules: Total working hours in 2024: (monthly working days) ╳ (number of employed 
and non-employed people) ╳ (daily working hours).
1. Occupational disease incidence rate (ODR) = (total number of occupational disease cases/total 
working hours) ╳ 200,000, no occupational diseases occurred.
2. The number of deaths due to work-related injuries during the reporting period was 0.
3. Disability injury severity rate (SR): number of days lost due to work-related injuries ╳ 1 million/total 
working hours.
4. Disability injury frequency rate (FR): number of occupational injuries ╳ 1 million/total working hours.
5. Total work-related injury rate = (total number of work-related injuries/total working hours) ╳ 200,000.

Appendix
Fire simulation drill/toxic disaster training course
After a disaster occurs, power outages may occur, resulting in poor visibility. 
When a large number of people evacuate, falls or stampedes are likely to occur. 
In order to prevent disasters, enhance self-response and protection capabilities, 
raise colleagues' disaster prevention awareness, and ensure smooth evacuation 
when disasters occur. In 2024, the Taiwan factory conducted three full-site fire 
safety drills and toxic disaster training courses to enhance colleagues' disaster 
prevention capabilities. The Shanghai and US factories each held two full-site 
emergency evacuation drills to strengthen crisis response capabilities when 
disasters occur, improve employee safety awareness and safe evacuation 
capabilities, and take various preventive measures before disasters occur. 
Evacuation and notification after a disaster can reduce the company's asset and 
manpower losses.
【2024 年台灣廠辦理消防/ 毒災訓練課程】
【2024 年上海廠辦理消防/ 毒災訓練課程】
【2024 年泰國廠辦理消防疏散訓練班】
Corporate Volunteer Firefighting Activities
Tainan City Fire Department actively promotes corporate volunteer firefighting. 
In view of the high risk of factory fires, Everest Industrial Co., Ltd. established 
a "fire brigade" in 2024 and organized personnel (divided into three groups, a 
total of 28 people) to respond to the corporate volunteer firefighting plan. The 
Fire Department's Fourth Disaster Rescue Team held an enlistment ceremony at 
Everest Industrial Co., Ltd., emphasizing the importance of "safeguarding one's 
own property" and assisting in training employees to improve initial firefighting 
and disaster rescue capabilities.
Everest Industrial Co., Ltd. provides fire brigade employees with public holiday 
training, allowances and overtime pay to encourage participation in disaster 
response efforts. The Fire Department hopes to encourage more manufacturers 
to participate through the corporate volunteer firefighting program, jointly 
improve Tainan City's firefighting capabilities, strengthen factory disaster 
response capabilities, and create a safer environment.
In response to the corporate volunteer firefighting recruitment plan promoted 
by the Fire Department, the company will be able to control the disaster 
situation, strengthen disaster response capabilities, and improve employees' 
4.3 Occupational Safety and Health
firefighting and disaster relief capabilities 
when a disaster occurs, thereby ensuring the 
safety of both the company and its employees. 
In addition to allowances and benefits, the 
company will also provide fire training public 
holidays and overtime subsidies for colleagues 
who assist in disaster relief. These six corporate 
volunteer firefighters were originally the "fire 
brigade" of the company's fire self-defense 
force. Textile factories contain a large amount 
of flammable materials and chemicals, 
making corporate disaster prevention and fire 
safety even more important. Participating in 
volunteer firefighting activities can not only 
help each other, but also cultivate employees' 
emergency response capabilities, reduce 
disaster losses, protect factories to achieve 
public safety, community stability, and protect 
the lives and property of employees.

Appendix
4.3.2 Workplace Health Promotion
Employee Health Management
Employees are the company's most valuable assets. We actively invest in health 
promotion resources and are committed to improving employees' physical 
and mental health and workplace safety. Our goal is to create a safer, more 
comfortable and friendly working environment so that every employee can fully 
realize their potential in a healthy working atmosphere.
In addition to formulating a comprehensive health promotion plan in 
accordance with regulations, we also conduct data analysis through the health 
management system, compare the results of health examinations over the 
years, and implement a comprehensive health management mechanism based 
on the type and severity of abnormalities, including hierarchical management, 
continuous tracking and professional medical consultation, to ensure that 
employees' health is effectively, systematically and continuously cared for.
Health management mechanism
In order to strengthen employees' awareness of health management, improve 
overall work ability, and reduce employees' occupational disease risks, the 
Environmental Safety Office implements job selection consultation (establishing 
health records, diseases that are not suitable for work in accordance with 
Appendix 8 of the Labor Health Protection Regulations), health screening 
(including physical and medical check-ups), health classification and management 
(health education, consultation, re-examination), job transfer, and return to work
The subjects cover both employees in service and transferred employees, 
ensuring that the health management of all employees is properly paid attention 
to.
Major health hazards and special health checks
The Taiwan factory identified the main health hazards as noise hazards in 
weaving mills and yarn processing factories, and chemical hazards in organic 
workplaces in post-processing, cutting-edge technology research institutes, 
and polyurethane factories. The Shanghai factory identified physical hazards 
such as noise hazards, wastewater treatment, and dyeing, as well as chemical 
hazards. The  American factory identified noise hazards in weaving mills and 
yarn processing factories. Special health checks were conducted on employees 
engaged in related operations. If abnormal health check values are found, in 
addition to providing health consultation guidance and follow-up management, 
education and training and the wearing of protective equipment are also 
strengthened.
Health Promotion and Education Training in 2024
The company organizes a number of safety, hygiene and health promotion 
education training to enhance employees' awareness and ability of workplace 
safety and health, and achieve the goal of physical, mental and spiritual health.
Taiwan factory health service doctors and occupational doctors 
regularly visit the factory to provide consultation services to 
Everest employees

4.4 Social Care and Public Welfare
4.4 Social Care and Public Welfare
GRI 2-28、SDGs4.7
Everest Sustainable Business Model
Everest Industrial adheres to the Far Eastern Group’s entrepreneurial spirit 
of "integrity, diligence, thrift, stability, and innovation" and is committed to 
creating shared value with stakeholders. The company adheres to the triple 
bottom line of economy, society, and environment, striving to build a sustainable 
enterprise that delivers win-win outcomes for employees, customers, suppliers, 
shareholders, society (community), and the environment. Everest promotes 
social progress and environmental protection while achieving economic benefits 
through honest management, hard work, simplicity, stable management, and 
continuous innovation. The company is dedicated to creating long-term value 
for all stakeholders and realizing common prosperity.
Community and Community Participation
In terms of social participation and public welfare sponsorship, Everest 
cooperates with domestic and international associations, non-profit 
organizations, and government agencies to promote related affairs, foster the 
harmonious development of industrial clusters and society, and demonstrate 
Everest’s humanistic care in a globalized society. The list of participating 
communities is as follows:

Appendix
Community Commitment and Action
Transparent Factory: Building community trust and safety, and 
promoting communication among stakeholders
Everest's grand transformation goal: Contribute to society and change the 
world. Fulfill corporate social responsibility and achieve a triple surplus of 
economy, society and environment.
Value proposition: Create shared value with stakeholders and become a 
sustainable and conscious enterprise that succeeds alongside employees, 
customers, suppliers, shareholders, society, and the environment.
In order to share Everest's innovative, sustainable, smart, and lean actions 
and achievements, the company has opened its Eco-Industrial Park to school 
groups, government agencies, and business partners for industry-university R&D 
and field visits. This allows for a deeper understanding of factory operations 
and environmental sustainability, helps build public trust, and encourages full 
interaction and communication to ensure the company's development aligns 
with market trends. It also fosters appreciation for technological advancements 
that drive industrial growth. At the same time, the Natural Fruit and Vegetable 
Education Farm, the Eco-Brick Factory and the MIT Automated Garment Factory 
Process are open to visitors. These practical experiences serve as practical 
exchange platforms for industry and environmental education, promoting 
the sustainable concept of triple surplus, and allowing visitors to witness the 
transformation and innovation of traditional factories in Taiwan's textile industry, 
as well as the improvement process of sustainable smart green factories.
In 2024, the company will focus on its core business and open fewer visiting 
groups, with 101 visitors. By the end of 2024, the cumulative number of visitors 
reached 15,718.

Community Care and Charity at the Thailand Factory
In 2024, the Everest Thailand Factory provided Children's Day funding and 
prize sponsorship through local schools to encourage children to learn and 
showcase their talents, making the activities more vibrant. It not only recognizes 
the children's efforts, but also helps the corporate image, enhances the 
harmonious development of society, understands the current needs of schools, 
and encouraged greater attention from both society and businesses to children's 
rights.
A healthy community is very important for enterprises. Everest actively 
contributes to the community and participates in various activities, helping 
village communities mow grass, tidying the surrounding environment, and 
improving the overall quality of life in the community. The company donates 
fabrics and funds for the Water Splashing Festival, sponsors temples, water 
lantern festival activities, Red Cross prizes, etc., and donates trial-dyed cloth 
to promote reuse and environmental sustainability, working with community 
residents to protect the environment and create a green home. The number of 
donated yards is 117,639. The Shanghai and US factories did not hold any related 
activities in 2024, and but plan to participate in various charity projects in the 
future.
List of sponsorships for various activities of the Thailand factory
Photos of the Thailand factory and local charity activities
Old shoes save lives and warm Africa
The company called on colleagues to participate in the "Happy Taiwan" 
fundraising and donation activities. Through the proceeds from charity sales 
and material donations, we support poor areas in Africa and people in need, 
bringing more resources and warmth to local communities while promoting 
environmental protection and public welfare efforts.
This is not only a charity fundraising, but also an opportunity to arouse the 
society's attention to vulnerable groups. The company hopes that through 
practical actions, Taiwan's compassion can be transformed into blessings and 
deliver warmth to every corner of the world in need.
Many developing countries face the challenges of urban-rural disparities and 
resource scarcity. This event not only demonstrates the social responsibility of 
enterprises, but is also an important step in promoting sustainable development 
and realizing social value. The company encourages employees to actively 
participate and looks forward to working with more public welfare partners in 
the future to bring more care and support to the world.

Appendix I: Overview of ESG Data
Appendix I: Overview of ESG Data
Greenhouse Gas Inventory Information
Air pollutants emissions unit: t
Remarks:
1. Types of greenhouse gas emissions: carbon dioxide (CO 2), methane (CH 4), nitrous oxide (N 2 O), hydrofluorocarbons 
(HFCs), sulfur hexafluoride (SF 6), perfluorocarbons (PFCs) and nitrogen trifluoride (NF3).
2. Scope of Statistics: A total of four sites; Method for Consolidating Greenhouse Gas Emissions: Operational Control
Approach.
3. The standards used are based on ISO/CNS 14064-1, ISO/CNS 14064-3.
4. Methodology used: Global Warming Potential (GWP) is calculated using the Global Warming Potential value, emission 
coefficient method and mass balance method on the IPCC Fifth Assessment Report (2007).
5. The source of the conversion coefficient used: the latest greenhouse gas emission coefficient management table
version 6.0.4 published by the Environmental Protection Administration of the Executive TWD. Indirect emissions
include purchased electricity, and the electricity emission coefficients are: Taiwan = 0.495 kgCO2e; Thailand = 0.4655 
kgCO2e; the United States = 0.408 kgCO2e. According to the Shanghai Municipal Ecological Environment Bureau’s
notice on adjusting the emission factor values related to the city’s greenhouse gas emission accounting guidelines: 
the electricity emission factor was adjusted from 7.88 t CO 2 /104 kWh to 4.2 t CO 2 /104 kWh, and the thermal
emission factor was adjusted from 0.11 t CO 2 /GJ is adjusted to 0.06 t CO 2 /GJ; the indirect emissions from the
Shanghai factory include the electricity used by the Baoan office.
6. In this factory, the M07, M09, and M10 processes use organic sludge (dried sludge) and Solid Recovered Fuel (SRF) as 
auxiliary fuels in coal-fired boilers. The greenhouse gas emissions from the combustion of biomass fuels within the
organizational boundary amounted to 1,686.1295 metric tons of CO2e.
7. Taiwan factory’s Scope 1 and 2 data passed ISO 14064 greenhouse gas inventory certification.
8. The greenhouse gas emissions from overseas factories have not yet been investigated and confirmed, and
explanations will be provided to each factory in the future.
Remark:
1. Taiwan factory data is reported to the Tainan City Environmental Protection Bureau and Environmental Protection
Administration in compliance with regulations, and is subject to annual spot inspections.
2. Shanghai factory data is disclosed through regular monitoring and calculation in accordance with the requirements of 
the pollution discharge permit. 
3. The U.S. factory will outsource monitoring and management in 2025; the reported figures are currently estimates.

GJ

Audit failure types (for common damage types in internal audits):.Taiwan factory: falling, collapsing 
objects, clamping, fire, electric shock, flying objects, contact with harmful substances, etc..
Remarks: 
2023: (working days per month) X (number of employees and non-employees) X (working hours per

4. Disabling injury severity rate (SR): number of days lost due to occupational injury*1000000/total
working hours
5. Disabling injury frequency rate (FR): number of occupational injuries * 1,000,000/total working hours
6. Total work-related injury rate = (total work-related injuries/total working hours) * 200,000

(II)SASB Industry Indicators — Chemicals
Dyeing, finishing, printing, and other processes require the use of chemicals. The 
company actively manages chemical usage and conducts inventories with reference to the 
SASB indicators of the chemical industry to mitigate the impact on the environment and 
address stakeholder concerns.
